Hausman Test - Market 1

\begin{verbatim}
## 
##  Hausman Test
## 
## data:  belief ~ p_trend
## chisq = 1199.1, df = 1, p-value < 2.2e-16
## alternative hypothesis: one model is inconsistent
\end{verbatim}

Hausman Test - Market 2

\begin{verbatim}
## 
##  Hausman Test
## 
## data:  belief ~ p_trend
## chisq = 1199.1, df = 1, p-value < 2.2e-16
## alternative hypothesis: one model is inconsistent
\end{verbatim}

(If the null is rejected, the Fixed effects method is chosen to model
the data instead of the Random effects method)

\hypertarget{observers-only}{%
\subsection{Observers only}\label{observers-only}}

 
  \providecommand{\huxb}[2]{\arrayrulecolor[RGB]{#1}\global\arrayrulewidth=#2pt}
  \providecommand{\huxvb}[2]{\color[RGB]{#1}\vrule width #2pt}
  \providecommand{\huxtpad}[1]{\rule{0pt}{\baselineskip+#1}}
  \providecommand{\huxbpad}[1]{\rule[-#1]{0pt}{#1}}

\begin{table}[h]

\begin{verbatim}
## 
##  Hausman Test
## 
## data:  belief ~ p_trend
## chisq = 297.94, df = 1, p-value < 2.2e-16
## alternative hypothesis: one model is inconsistent
\end{verbatim}

\end{verbatim}

the data instead of the Random effects method)

## 
##  Hausman Test
## 
## data:  belief ~ p_trend

\end{verbatim}

## alternative hypothesis: one model is inconsistent
\end{verbatim}

(If the null is rejected, the Fixed effects method is chosen to model
the data instead of the Random effects method)

Hausman Test - Market 1

\begin{verbatim}
## 
##  Hausman Test
## 
## data:  belief ~ p_trend + traders_1
## chisq = 7.6396, df = 1, p-value = 0.00571
## alternative hypothesis: one model is inconsistent
\end{verbatim}

Hausman Test - Market 2

\begin{verbatim}
## 
##  Hausman Test
## 
## data:  belief ~ p_trend + traders_1
## chisq = 7.6396, df = 1, p-value = 0.00571
## alternative hypothesis: one model is inconsistent
\end{verbatim}

(If the null is rejected, the Fixed effects method is chosen to model
the data instead of the Random effects method)

Hausman Test - Market 1

\begin{verbatim}
## 
##  Hausman Test
## 
## data:  belief ~ p_trend + traders_1
## chisq = 719.66, df = 1, p-value < 2.2e-16
## alternative hypothesis: one model is inconsistent
\end{verbatim}

Hausman Test - Market 2

\begin{verbatim}
## 
##  Hausman Test
## 
## data:  belief ~ p_trend + traders_1
## chisq = 719.66, df = 1, p-value < 2.2e-16
## alternative hypothesis: one model is inconsistent
\end{verbatim}

(If the null is rejected, the Fixed effects method is chosen to model
the data instead of the Random effects method)

##

\end{verbatim}

##

## chisq = 15.041, df = 1, p-value = 0.0001052
## alternative hypothesis: one model is inconsistent
\end{verbatim}

(If the null is rejected, the Fixed effects method is chosen to model
the data instead of the Random effects method)

\hypertarget{dummy-variable-6}{%
\subsection{Dummy variable}\label{dummy-variable-6}}

 
  \providecommand{\huxb}[2]{\arrayrulecolor[RGB]{#1}\global\arrayrulewidth=#2pt}

Hausman Test - Market 1

\begin{verbatim}
## 
##  Hausman Test
## 
## data:  belief ~ p_trend + traders_1
## chisq = 48.007, df = 2, p-value = 3.762e-11
## alternative hypothesis: one model is inconsistent
\end{verbatim}

Hausman Test - Market 2

\begin{verbatim}
## 
##  Hausman Test
## 
## data:  belief ~ p_trend + traders_1
## chisq = 48.007, df = 2, p-value = 3.762e-11
## alternative hypothesis: one model is inconsistent
\end{verbatim}

(If the null is rejected, the Fixed effects method is chosen to model
the data instead of the Random effects method)
